# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: rust_ml_computer_vision_expert_054_architectural_understanding_expert_01

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis for Microservice Extraction in VisuTility Orchestrator

## Description

VisuTility Orchestrator is a complex, monolithic Rust application for managing computer vision MLOps pipelines. Due to its success, the business wants to offer its powerful experiment tracking capabilities as a standalone, cloud-native product. This requires extracting the relevant logic into a new, independent microservice. The current codebase is large and complex, with module names obfuscated, requiring deep analysis to untangle dependencies. The task is to perform the initial architectural analysis to plan this extraction.

## Your Task

You are a senior software architect. Your goal is to analyze the 'VisuTility Orchestrator' codebase and produce a plan for extracting the 'experiment_tracking' feature into a separate microservice. You must not write any new code, but provide a detailed architectural report.

Your report must contain four sections:

1.  **Core Component Identification:** Identify the primary Rust modules (e.g., `src/module_XX.txt`) that constitute the core logic for experiment tracking. This includes managing experiments, runs, logging metrics, parameters, and artifacts.

2.  **Dependency Analysis:** Create a dependency map for the identified core components. This map should detail:
    *   **Internal Dependencies:** Which other modules within the monolith do the core experiment tracking modules depend on (e.g., database connectors, shared data structures, configuration loaders)?
    *   **External Consumers:** Which other modules in the monolith consume the services of the experiment tracking components (e.g., model training or hyperparameter tuning modules that need to log their results)?

3.  **Proposed Service API:** Define a high-level, language-agnostic RESTful API for the new 'Experiment Tracking' microservice. The API should expose all necessary functionalities currently provided internally. Specify the resources, endpoints, HTTP methods, and expected request/response payloads (in brief).

4.  **Refactoring Plan:** List the specific modules within the remaining monolith that will require modification to use the new microservice API instead of the current internal calls. For each module, briefly describe the nature of the change required.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this task systematically:

1.  **Keyword-based Search:** Perform a global search across all `src/*.txt` files for keywords related to experiment tracking, such as `experiment`, `run`, `metric`, `parameter`, `log_metric`, `log_param`, `artifact`, `start_run`, `end_run`.
2.  **Module Triaging:** Analyze the search results to identify a small set of modules with the highest concentration and relevance of these keywords. These are the likely core components.
3.  **Dependency Tracing (Internal):** For each identified core module, inspect its `use` statements and function calls to other modules. This will reveal its dependencies on shared utilities like database clients (`db::`), configuration (`config::`), or common data types (`types::`).
4.  **Dependency Tracing (External):** Use IDE tools or command-line searches (like `grep`) to find all usages of the public functions, structs, and traits defined in the core experiment tracking modules. The files containing these usages are the 'External Consumers'.
5.  **API Synthesis:** Based on the functions exposed by the core modules (e.g., `create_experiment`, `log_metric_to_run`, `get_run_details`), synthesize a logical, resource-oriented RESTful API. Common patterns would be `POST /runs` to create, `PATCH /runs/{id}` to update (e.g., log metrics), and `GET /runs/{id}` to retrieve.
6.  **Consolidation:** Compile the findings into the four requested sections. The 'Refactoring Plan' would be directly derived from the list of 'External Consumers' identified in step 4.

## Evaluation Criteria

- {'name': 'Correctness of Core Component Identification', 'description': 'Agent correctly identifies a plausible set of modules responsible for experiment tracking, based on code analysis.'}
- {'name': 'Accuracy of Dependency Mapping', 'description': 'Agent correctly identifies both key modules that are depended upon (e.g., DB, config) and key modules that are consumers (e.g., training, tuning).'}
- {'name': 'Quality and Completeness of API Design', 'description': 'The proposed API is well-structured, RESTful, and covers the essential functionalities of creating runs and logging data. The design is logical and practical.'}
- {'name': 'Viability of Refactoring Plan', 'description': 'The agent correctly identifies the modules that need to be refactored and accurately describes the nature of the required changes (i.e., replacing internal calls with API calls).'}
- {'name': 'Clarity of Rationale', 'description': 'The agent provides clear justifications for its conclusions, referencing evidence from the codebase to support its identification of modules and dependencies.'}

     1→```rust
     2→//! src/constants.rs
     3→//!
     4→//! Global, application-wide constants for the _VisuTility Orchestrator_ project.
     5→//!
     6→//! This module centralises all “magic numbers”, environment-variable names,
     7→//! default network ports, timeouts, and other immutable settings that are
     8→//! consumed across multiple layers of the code-base.  Co-locating them here
     9→//! helps to keep the rest of the implementation tidy and makes it trivial to
    10→//! discover and change process-wide parameters.
    11→//!
    12→//! ## Usage
    13→//!
    14→//! ```rust
    15→//! use visutility_orchestrator::constants::*;
    16→//!
    17→//! let addr = *DEFAULT_HTTP_SOCKET_ADDR;       // 0.0.0.0:7812
    18→//! let ns   = MODEL_REGISTRY_NAMESPACE;        // "visutility"
    19→//! ```
    20→//!
    21→//! ## Conventions
    22→//!
    23→//! 1. Immutable, compile-time literals are uppercase `const`s.
    24→//! 2. Values that must be computed at startup (e.g. Regex, Duration) are
    25→//!    exposed as `Lazy` statics (`once_cell`).
    26→//! 3. All string constants meant for environment variables are suffixed with
    27→//!    `_ENV` (e.g. `DATABASE_URL_ENV`).
    28→
    29→use once_cell::sync::Lazy;
    30→use regex::Regex;
    31→use std::{
    32→    net::SocketAddr,
    33→    time::Duration,
    34→};
    35→
    36→/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */
    37→/*                               Build Metadata                               */
    38→/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */
    39→
    40→/// Crate semantic version, injected by Cargo at compile-time.
    41→pub const BUILD_SEMVER: &str = env!("CARGO_PKG_VERSION");
    42→
    43→///

119-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis for the Experiment Tracking microservice extraction. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I analyzed the VisuTility Orchestrator codebase (78 Rust modules) and identified:

### Core Experiment Tracking Modules (4 modules):
1. **module_12.txt** - Primary in-memory tracker with `ExperimentTracker`, `ExperimentRun`, `TrainingEvent`, async broadcast channels
2. **module_71.txt** - SQLite-backed persistent tracker with `rusqlite`
3. **module_20.txt** - File-based tracker with `EventBus` and `LocalFileTracker`
4. **module_25.txt** - Multi-backend tracker (File/HTTP) with `TrackerFactory`

### Key Dependencies:
- **Internal**: `utils.txt` (event bus, config), `config.txt`, `constants.txt`
- **External crates**: tokio, serde, rusqlite, chrono, uuid, thiserror, broadcast channels

### Consumer Modules (11 modules):
- module_2, 4, 13, 27, 33, 34, 53, 54, 62, 76, 78 - all use experiment tracking for hyperparameter tuning, model monitoring, and automated retraining

### Proposed REST API:
A comprehensive RESTful API with endpoints for:
- Experiments (CRUD)
- Runs (start, end, list)
- Metrics (log, retrieve)
- Parameters (get, update)
- Artifacts (upload, download)
- WebSocket events for real-time streaming

### Refactoring Plan:
Detailed changes required for each of the 11 consumer modules to switch from internal calls to HTTP/WebSocket API calls, with a 4-phase migration strategy.

The complete report is available at `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

It provides two core capabilities:\n//!  1. Strategy-based hyper-parameter tuning (currently Random Search,\n//!     but additional strategies can be plugged in at runtime).\n//!  2. Thread-safe, observer-friendly experiment tracking that can be\n//!     queried by other layers (e.g. Model Registry, Monitoring).\n//!\n//! Design patterns in play\n//! -----------------------\n//! \u2022 Strategy Pattern  \u2013 `HyperParamTuner` (trait) + concrete impls.  \n//! \u2022 Observer Pattern  \u2013 `TrainingEvent` + `TrainingObserver` for model\n//!                       monitoring / automated retraining triggers.\n//! \u2022 Factory Pattern   \u2013 The `TunerFactory` decides which strategy to\n//!                       instantiate based on runtime config.\n//!\n//! UnknownStrategy(String),\n        #[error(\"Experiment run not found: {0}\")]\n        UnknownRun(Uuid),\n        #[error(\"Metric key already exists in this step: {0}\")]\n        DuplicateMetricKey(String),\n        #[error(\"Serialization error: {0}\")]\n        SerdeError(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n        #[error(\"Internal error: {0}\")]\n        Internal(String),\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nmod observer {\n    use super::*;\n\n    /// Observable events emitted by the training loop.\n    #[derive(Debug, Clone)]\n    pub enum TrainingEvent {\n        EpochEnd {\n            run_id: Uuid,\n            epoch: usize,\n            metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n            timestamp: SystemTime,\n        },\n        TrainingEnd {\n            run_id: Uuid,\n            final_metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n            duration: Duration,\n            timestamp: SystemTime,\n        },\n    }\n\n    /// Observer trait that other layers can implement to react to events.\n    pub trait TrainingObserver: Send + Sync {\n        fn on_event(&self, event: &TrainingEvent);\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nmod tracker {\n    use super::*;\n\n    /// Metadata for one experiment run.\n    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n    pub struct ExperimentRun {\n        pub run_id: Uuid,\n        pub params: HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n        pub start_time: SystemTime,\n        pub end_time: Option<SystemTime>,\n        pub metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n        pub tags: Vec<String>,\n    }\n\n    /// Thread-safe experiment tracker that broadcasts events to observers.\n    #[derive(Clone)]\n    pub struct ExperimentTracker {\n        state: Arc<RwLock<HashMap<Uuid, ExperimentRun>>>,\n        broadcaster: broadcast::Sender<TrainingEvent>,\n    }\n\n    impl ExperimentTracker {\n        pub fn new() -> Self {\n            // 32 is an arbitrary channel size; adjust to throughput needs.\n            let (tx, _) = broadcast::channel(32);\n            Self {\n                state: Arc::new(RwLock::new(HashMap::new())),\n                broadcaster: tx,\n            }\n        }\n\n        /// Subscribe to training events.\n        pub fn subscribe(&self) -> broadcast::Receiver<TrainingEvent> {\n            self.broadcaster.subscribe()\n        }\n\n        /// Start a new run with given parameters. Returns run_id.\n        pub async fn start_run(\n            &self,\n            params: HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n            tags: Vec<String>,\n        ) -> Uuid {\n            let run = ExperimentRun {\n                run_id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n                params,\n                start_time: SystemTime::now(),\n                end_time: None,\n                metrics: HashMap::new(),\n                tags,\n            };\n            let run_id = run.run_id;\n            self.state.write().await.insert(run_id, run);\n            run_id\n        }\n\n        /// Log metrics for a run & epoch, broadcasting an event.\n        pub async fn log_epoch_metrics(\n            &self,\n            run_id: Uuid,\n            epoch: usize,\n            metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n        ) -> Result<(), TunerError> {\n            let mut state = self.state.write().await;\n            let run = state\n                .get_mut(&run_id)\n                .ok_or_else(|| TunerError::UnknownRun(run_id))?;\n\n            // Merge metrics into current map (overwrite duplicates).\n            for (k, v) in &metrics {\n                run.metrics.insert(k.clone(), *v);\n            }\n\n            let event = TrainingEvent::EpochEnd {\n                run_id,\n                epoch,\n                metrics,\n                timestamp: SystemTime::now(),\n            };\n            let _ = self.broadcaster.send(event); // Ignore if no receivers.\n            Ok(())\n        }\n\n        /// Finalize a run, compute its duration & send final event.\n        pub async fn end_run(\n            &self,\n            run_id: Uuid,\n            final_metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n        ) -> Result<(), TunerError> {\n            let mut state = self.state.write().await;\n            let run = state\n                .get_mut(&run_id)\n                .ok_or_else(|| TunerError::UnknownRun(run_id))?;\n\n            run.end_time = Some(SystemTime::now());\n            for (k, v) in &final_metrics {\n                run.metrics.insert(k.clone(), *v);\n            }\n\n            let duration = run\n                .end_time\n                .unwrap()\n                .duration_since(run.start_time)\n                .unwrap_or_default();\n\n            let event = TrainingEvent::TrainingEnd {\n                run_id,\n                final_metrics,\n                duration,\n                timestamp: SystemTime::now(),\n            };\n            let _ = self.broadcaster.send(event);\n            Ok(())\n        }\n\n        /// A cheap read-only snapshot of a completed run.\n        pub async fn get_run(&self, run_id: Uuid) -> Option<ExperimentRun> {\n            self.state.read().await.get(&run_id).cloned()\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nmod tuner {\n    use super::*;\n\n    // ---------------------- Hyper-parameter specification ------------------\n    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n    #[serde(untagged)]\n    pub enum HyperParamValue {\n        Int(i64),\n        Float(f64),\n        Text(String),\n        Flag(bool),\n    }\n\n    impl fmt::Display for HyperParamValue {\n        fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n            match self {\n                HyperParamValue::Int(v) => write!(f, \"{}\", v),\n                HyperParamValue::Float(v) => write!(f, \"{}\", v),\n                HyperParamValue::Text(v) => write!(f, \"{}\", v),\n                HyperParamValue::Flag(v) => write!(f, \"{}\", v),\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Parameter space configuration (search domain).\n    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n    #[serde(tag = \"type\", rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\n    pub enum HyperParamSpec {\n        IntRange { min: i64, max: i64 },\n        FloatRange { min: f64, max: f64 },\n        Choice { options: Vec<String> },\n        Flag,\n    }\n\n    // -------------------------- Strategy Trait ----------------------------\n    #[async_trait::async_trait]\n    pub trait HyperParamTuner: Send + Sync {\n        /// Produce the next candidate configuration.\n        async fn suggest(&self) -> HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>;\n\n        /// Notify the tuner of the evaluation result so underlying\n        /// strategies can update their priors.\n        async fn record_result(\n            &self,\n            params: HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n            score: f64,\n        ) -> Result<(), TunerError>;\n\n        /// Optional JSON snapshot for auditability.\n        async fn snapshot(&self) -> Result<String, TunerError>;\n    }\n\n    // ---------------------- Random Search Strategy ------------------------\n    pub struct RandomSearchTuner {\n        specs: HashMap<String, HyperParamSpec>,\n        rng: RwLock<StdRng>,\n    }\n\n    impl RandomSearchTuner {\n        pub fn new(specs: HashMap<String, HyperParamSpec>) -> Self {\n            Self {\n                specs,\n                rng: RwLock::new(StdRng::from_entropy()),\n            }\n        }\n\n        fn sample_from_spec(\n            spec: &HyperParamSpec,\n            rng: &mut StdRng,\n        ) -> HyperParamValue {\n            match spec {\n                HyperParamSpec::IntRange { min, max } => {\n                    let dist = Uniform::new_inclusive(*min, *max);\n                    HyperParamValue::Int(rng.sample(dist))\n                }\n                HyperParamSpec::FloatRange { min, max } => {\n                    let dist = Uniform::new_inclusive(*min, *max);\n                    HyperParamValue::Float(rng.sample(dist))\n                }\n                HyperParamSpec::Choice { options } => {\n                    let idx = rng.gen_range(0..options.len());\n                    HyperParamValue::Text(options[idx].clone())\n                }\n                HyperParamSpec::Flag => HyperParamValue::Flag(rng.gen::<bool>()),\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait::async_trait]\n    impl HyperParamTuner for RandomSearchTuner {\n        async fn suggest(&self) -> HashMap<String, HyperParamValue> {\n            let mut rng = self.rng.write().await;\n            self.specs\n                .iter()\n                .map(|(k, spec)| (k.clone(), Self::sample_from_spec(spec, &mut rng)))\n                .collect()\n        }\n\n        async fn record_result(\n            &self,\n            _params: HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n            _score: f64,\n        ) -> Result<(), TunerError> {\n            // Random Search does not learn from feedback.\n            Ok(())\n        }\n\n        async fn snapshot(&self) -> Result<String, TunerError> {\n            serde_json::to_string(&self.specs)\n                .map_err(TunerError::from)\n        }\n    }\n\n    // ------------------------ Factory for Tuners --------------------------\n    pub enum TunerFactory;\n\n    impl TunerFactory {\n        /// Instantiate a tuner from JSON config.\n        pub fn build(\n            strategy: &str,\n            specs: HashMap<String, HyperParamSpec>,\n        ) -> Result<Box<dyn HyperParamTuner>, TunerError> {\n            match strategy.to_lowercase().as_str() {\n                \"random_search\" | \"random\" => Ok(Box::new(RandomSearchTuner::new(specs))),\n                other => Err(TunerError::UnknownStrategy(other.to_string())),\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Example usage (to be compiled out in production)\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::time::Duration;\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn smoke_test_random_search_and_tracker() {\n        // 1. Build tuner\n        let mut specs = HashMap::new();\n        specs.insert(\n            \"learning_rate\".into(),\n            HyperParamSpec::FloatRange { min: 1e-4, max: 1e-1 },\n        );\n        specs.insert(\n            \"num_layers\".into(),\n            HyperParamSpec::IntRange { min: 1, max: 6 },\n        );\n        let tuner = TunerFactory::build(\"random\", specs).unwrap();\n\n        // 2. Create tracker & subscribe to events\n        let tracker = ExperimentTracker::new();\n        let mut rx = tracker.subscribe();\n\n        // 3. Suggest parameters & start run\n        let params = tuner.suggest().await;\n        let run_id = tracker.start_run(params.clone(), vec![\"integration-test\".into()]).await;\n\n        // Simulate training loop\n        for epoch in 0..3 {\n            // Fake some metric\n            let mut metrics = HashMap::new();\n            metrics.insert(\"loss\".into(), 1.0 / (epoch as f64 + 1.0));\n            tracker.log_epoch_metrics(run_id, epoch, metrics).await.unwrap();\n            tokio::time::sleep(Duration::from_millis(10)).await;\n        }\n\n        // End run\n        let mut final_metrics = HashMap::new();\n        final_metrics.insert(\"accuracy\".into(), 0.85);\n        tracker.end_run(run_id, final_metrics.clone()).await.unwrap();\n\n        // Consume events\n        let mut epoch_events = 0;\n        while let Ok(event) = rx.try_recv() {\n            match event {\n                TrainingEvent::EpochEnd { .. } => epoch_events += 1,\n                TrainingEvent::TrainingEnd { final_metrics: m, .. } => {\n                    assert_eq!(m.get(\"accuracy\"), final_metrics.get(\"accuracy\"));\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        assert_eq!(epoch_events, 3);\n    }\n}\n```",

-------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Generic representation of a model\u2019s hyper-parameters.\n///\n/// Internally we store a `serde_json::Value` for flexibility, but typed\n/// accessor helpers are provided for ergonomics in business-logic code.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct HyperParameters {\n    inner: serde_json::Value,\n}\n\nimpl HyperParameters {\n    pub fn new(inner: serde_json::Value) -> Self {\n        Self { inner }\n    }\n\n    /// Convenience helper to get a numeric parameter.\n    pub fn get_f64(&self, key: &str) -> Option<f64> {\n        self.inner\n            .get(key)\n            .and_then(|v| v.as_f64())\n    }\n\n    /// Convenience helper to set/update a parameter.\n    pub fn set<K: Into<String>, T: Serialize>(&mut self, key: K, value: T) -> Result<()> {\n        let mut map = self\n            .inner\n            .as_object()\n            .cloned()\n            .unwrap_or_else(|| serde_json::Map::new());\n        map.insert(\n            key.into(),\n            serde_json::to_value(value).context(\"serializing parameter\")?,\n        );\n        self.inner = serde_json::Value::Object(map);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Metrics reported by a running model.\n///\n/// For brevity we only capture a handful of metrics. In production, metrics\n/// would be routed from Prometheus/OpenTelemetry exporters.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ModelMetrics {\n    pub model_id: String,\n    pub accuracy: f64,\n    pub precision: f64,\n    pub recall: f64,\n    pub throughput_fps: f64,\n}\n\n/// Abstract capabilities that the Model-Ops layer must expose so that\n/// hyper-parameter tuning and re-training can be orchestrated independently\n/// of the underlying ML framework (e.g. TensorFlow, PyTorch, ONNX-Runtime).\npub trait ModelOps: Send + Sync {\n    /// Kick off an asynchronous re-training job for `model_id` using the\n    /// supplied hyper-parameters. The implementation is responsible for\n    /// returning immediately (non-blocking) and for emitting its own events\n    /// (status, success, failure) through the system\u2019s event bus.\n    fn retrain(&self, model_id: &str, params: HyperParameters) -> Result<()>;\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                          Strategy: Hyper-parameter Tuner                   */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Search space descriptor for na\u00efve grid-search.\n///\n/// More advanced tuners (e.g. Bayesian) would define their own descriptor.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct HyperParamSpace {\n    pub lr: Vec<f64>,\n    pub batch_size: Vec<u32>,\n    pub dropout: Vec<f64>,\n}\n\n/// Strategy interface for selecting the next candidate hyper-parameters.\npub trait HyperParameterTuner: Send + Sync {\n    /// Returns a new set of hyper-parameters based on the latest model metrics.\n    fn suggest(&mut self, metrics: &ModelMetrics) -> Option<HyperParameters>;\n}\n\n/// Reference strategy: exhaustive grid-search with random walk.\n///\n/// In production we would enumerate deterministically; here we randomise to\n/// avoid massive search space exploration in the example code.\npub struct GridSearchTuner {\n    /// Search grid catalogued in a naive way. For large search spaces, a\n    /// smarter iterator would be required.\n    grid: Vec<HyperParameters>,\n    /// Keep track of which configurations have been tried.\n    tried: HashMap<String, ()>,\n}\n\nimpl GridSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(space: HyperParamSpace) -> Self {\n        let mut grid = Vec::new();\n        for lr in space.lr {\n            for batch in &space.batch_size {\n                for dropout in &space.dropout {\n                    let params = serde_json::json!({\n                        \"learning_rate\": lr,\n                        \"batch_size\": batch,\n                        \"dropout\": dropout,\n                    });\n                    grid.push(HyperParameters::new(params));\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        Self {\n            grid,\n            tried: HashMap::new(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl HyperParameterTuner for GridSearchTuner {\n    fn suggest(&mut self, metrics: &ModelMetrics) -> Option<HyperParameters> {\n        // If the model performs well enough, no need to tune.\n        if metrics.accuracy >= 0.97 {\n            info!(\n                \"Model [{}] already meets accuracy target ({}). Skipping suggestion.\",\n                metrics.model_id, metrics.accuracy\n            );\n            return None;\n        }\n\n        // Otherwise, randomly take an unseen configuration from the grid.\n        let mut rng = thread_rng();\n        self.grid.shuffle(&mut rng);\n\n        for params in &self.grid {\n            let fingerprint = serde_json::to_string(&params).ok()?;\n            if !self.tried.contains_key(&fingerprint) {\n                info!(\n                    \"Suggesting new hyper-parameters for model [{}]: {}\",\n                    metrics.model_id, fingerprint\n                );\n                self.tried.insert(fingerprint, ());\n                return Some(params.clone());\n            }\n        }\n\n        info!(\n            \"Grid exhausted for model [{}]; no more hyper-parameters to try.\",\n            metrics.model_id\n        );\n        None\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                       Observer: Metric-driven Re-trainer                   */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// A generic observer that reacts to model metrics.\n///\n/// In a real-world system this trait would likely come from a common\n/// crate so that multiple modules can subscribe to events uniformly.\npub trait MetricsObserver: Send + Sync {\n    fn on_metrics(&self, metrics: ModelMetrics);\n}\n\n/// Central hub that receives incoming metrics and dispatches them to\n/// registered observers. This plays the *Subject* role in the Observer pattern.\npub struct MetricMonitor {\n    observers: Arc<Mutex<Vec<Arc<dyn MetricsObserver>>>>,\n    sender: Sender<ModelMetrics>,\n    _worker_handle: thread::JoinHandle<()>,\n}\n\nimpl MetricMonitor {\n    /// Creates a new monitor with a background worker thread that forwards\n    /// metrics to observers. The channel is bounded to apply back-pressure in\n    /// pathological cases.\n    pub fn new(buffer: usize) -> Self {\n        let observers = Arc::new(Mutex::new(Vec::new()));\n        let (sender, receiver) = bounded::<ModelMetrics>(buffer);\n        let observers_clone = observers.clone();\n\n        let handle = thread::spawn(move || Self::run(receiver, observers_clone));\n\n        Self {\n            observers,\n            sender,\n            _worker_handle: handle,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Internal worker loop.\n    fn run(receiver: Receiver<ModelMetrics>, observers: Arc<Mutex<Vec<Arc<dyn MetricsObserver>>>>) {\n        for metrics in receiver.iter() {\n            debug!(\"MetricMonitor received metrics: {:?}\", metrics);\n            let snapshot = {\n                // Take a snapshot to minimise lock contention duration.\n                observers.lock().unwrap().clone()\n            };\n            for obs in snapshot {\n                obs.on_metrics(metrics.clone());\n            }\n        }\n        info!(\"MetricMonitor worker terminating\");\n    }\n\n    /// Register a new observer.\n    pub fn subscribe<O: MetricsObserver + 'static>(&self, observer: O) {\n        self.observers.lock().unwrap().push(Arc::new(observer));\n    }\n\n    /// Feed metrics into the monitor. Called by the system\u2019s telemetry layer.\n    pub fn ingest(&self, metrics: ModelMetrics) {\n        if let Err(e) = self.sender.send(metrics) {\n            // Inbound side; losing metrics is severe \u2013 always log an error.\n            error!(\"Failed to dispatch metrics: {}\", e);\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                  Observer Implementation: Retrain Trigger                  */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Observer that decides when to trigger re-training based on metrics and\n/// delegates hyper-parameter suggestion to an injected tuner (Strategy).\npub struct RetrainTrigger<T: HyperParameterTuner> {\n    tuner: Mutex<T>,\n    model_ops: Arc<dyn ModelOps>,\n    /// Minimal gap (in seconds) between consecutive retraining events for the\n    /// same model. Prevents runaway retraining loops.\n    cooldown_secs: u64,\n    /// Track last retrain timestamp per model.\n    last_retrain: Mutex<HashMap<String, std::time::Instant>>,\n}\n\nimpl<T> RetrainTrigger<T>\nwhere\n    T: HyperParameterTuner + 'static,\n{\n    pub fn new(tuner: T, model_ops: Arc<dyn ModelOps>, cooldown_secs: u64) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            tuner: Mutex::new(tuner),\n            model_ops,\n            cooldown_secs,\n            last_retrain: Mutex::new(HashMap::new()),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<T> MetricsObserver for RetrainTrigger<T>\nwhere\n    T: HyperParameterTuner + 'static,\n{\n    fn on_metrics(&self, metrics: ModelMetrics) {\n        let now = std::time::Instant::now();\n\n        // Respect cooldown.\n        {\n            let mut map = self.last_retrain.lock().unwrap();\n            if let Some(last) = map.get(&metrics.model_id) {\n                if now.duration_since(*last).as_secs() < self.cooldown_secs {\n                    debug!(\n                        \"Cooldown active for model [{}], skipping retrain\",\n                        metrics.model_id\n                    );\n                    return;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Ask the strategy for new hyper-parameters.\n        let maybe_params = {\n            let mut tuner = self.tuner.lock().unwrap();\n            tuner.suggest(&metrics)\n        };\n\n        if let Some(params) = maybe_params {\n            info!(\n                \"Triggering re-training for model [{}] with new parameters\",\n                metrics.model_id\n            );\n            match self.model_ops.retrain(&metrics.model_id, params) {\n                Ok(_) => {\n                    self.last_retrain\n                        .lock()\n                        .unwrap()\n                        .insert(metrics.model_id.clone(), now);\n                    info!(\"Re-training job submitted successfully\");\n                }\n                Err(e) => {\n                    error!(\"Failed to submit re-training job: {:?}\", e);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                       Minimal Mock Implementations                         */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// A stub implementation that simulates a long-running re-training job.\n/// Useful for smoke-testing the observer without touching external systems.\npub struct MockModelOps;\n\nimpl ModelOps for MockModelOps {\n    fn retrain(&self, model_id: &str, params: HyperParameters) -> Result<()> {\n        let fingerprint = serde_json::to_string(&params)?;\n        // Spawn a detached thread so we don\u2019t block the caller.\n        let id = model_id.to_owned();\n        thread::spawn(move || {\n            info!(\n                \"Retraining [{}] in background with params: {}\",\n                id, fingerprint\n            );\n            thread::sleep(Duration::from_secs(3));\n            info!(\"Retraining [{}] finished\", id);\n        });\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                                 Unit Tests                                 */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::time::Instant;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn basic_end_to_end_flow() {\n        let monitor = MetricMonitor::new(8);\n        let space = HyperParamSpace {\n            lr: vec![0.01, 0.001],\n            batch_size: vec![8, 16],\n            dropout: vec![0.1, 0.2],\n        };\n        let tuner = GridSearchTuner::new(space);\n        let model_ops = Arc::new(MockModelOps);\n\n        let trigger = RetrainTrigger::new(tuner, model_ops, 1);\n        monitor.subscribe(trigger);\n\n        let metrics = ModelMetrics {\n            model_id: \"model-123\".into(),\n            accuracy: 0.80,\n            precision: 0.75,\n            recall: 0.78,\n            throughput_fps: 35.0,\n        };\n\n        let start = Instant::now();\n        monitor.ingest(metrics);\n\n        // Allow background job to complete.\n        while start.elapsed().as_secs() < 5 {\n            thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(200));\n        }\n    }\n}\n```",

Strategy-Pattern hyper-parameter tuning algorithms that leverage the\n//!    latest metrics to propose improved configurations.\n//!\n//! Key concepts implemented below:\n//! \u2022 ModelMetrics          \u2013 Lightweight, serializable metrics snapshot.\n//! \u2022 MetricsPublisher      \u2013 Observable broadcaster (tokio::broadcast).\n//! \u2022 HyperparameterTuner   \u2013 Strategy trait with async proposal interface.\n//! \u2022 GridTuner/BayesianTuner \u2013 Two concrete strategy implementations.\n//! \u2022 TunerFactory          \u2013 Factory-Pattern for runtime strategy selection.\n//! \u2022 AutoTuningService     \u2013 End-to-end orchestrator that wires everything up.\n//!\n//! Author: VisuTility Core Team\n//!            */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Buffer size used for the broadcast channel.\nconst METRICS_BUFFER: usize = 128;\n\n/// Component     if let Err(err) = self.inner.send(metrics) {\n            warn!(\"MetricsPublisher: failed to broadcast metrics: {err}\");\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Register a new subscriber for the metrics augmentation_prob: f32,\n}\n\nimpl Default for HyperParams {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            learning_rate: 3e-4,\n            weight_decay: 1e-2,\n            batch_size: 32,\n            augmentation_prob: 0.5,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Behaviour that each tuning strategy must implement.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait HyperparameterTuner: Send + Sync {\n    /// Consume recent metrics & propose a new hyper-parameters set.\n    async fn propose(\n        &mut self,\n        latest_metrics: &ModelMetrics,\n    ) -> Result<HyperParams>;\n\n    /// Optional hook so that {\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        // Build a tiny but combinatorically diverse grid.\n        let learning_rates = vec![1e-3, 3e-4, 1e-4];\n        let weight_decays = vec![1e-1, 1e-2];\n        let batch_sizes = vec![16, 32, 64];\n        let aug_probs = vec![0.3, 0.5, 0.8];\n\n        let mut grid = Vec::new();\n        for lr in &learning_rates {\n            for wd in &weight_decays {\n                for bs in &batch_sizes {\n                    for ap in &aug_probs {\n                        grid.push(HyperParams {\n                            learning_rate: *lr,\n                            weight_decay: *wd,\n                            batch_size: *bs,\n                            augmentation_prob: *ap,\n                        });\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        Self { grid, cursor: 0 }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl HyperparameterTuner for GridTuner {\n    async fn propose(\n        &mut self,\n        _latest_metrics: &ModelMetrics,\n    ) -> Result<HyperParams> {\n        if self.cursor >= self.grid.len() {\n            return Err(anyhow!(\"GridTuner has exhausted its search space\"));\n        }\n        let proposal = self.grid[self.cursor].clone();\n        self.cursor += 1;\n        Ok(proposal)\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"GridTuner\"\n    }\n}\n\n/* --------------------- Concrete Strategy: Bayesian Tuner ------------------ */\n\n/// Crude Bayesian optimisation tuner using a Gaussian-like exploration.\n/// In production we would leverage a dedicated crate (e.g., `bayes_opt`),\n/// but for this reference implementation we keep it self-contained.\npub struct BayesianTuner {\n    rng: ThreadRng,\n    /// History of tried params and their resulting accuracy so we can\n    /// bias towards the best ones (simplified Thompson Sampling).\n    history: VecDeque<(HyperParams, f32 /* accuracy */)>,\n    /// Maximum amount of history entries to keep in memory.\n    history_capacity: usize,\n}\n\nimpl BayesianTuner {\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            rng: rand::thread_rng(),\n            history: VecDeque::new(),\n            history_capacity: 200,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Internal helper that returns a weighted sampling distribution over\n    /// previous params (higher accuracy \u2192 higher weight).\n    fn weighted_sample(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams> {\n        if self.history.is_empty() {\n            return None;\n        }\n        // Build CDF based on accuracy.\n        let total_acc: f32 = self.history.iter().map(|(_, acc)| acc).sum();\n        if total_acc == 0.0 {\n            return None;\n        }\n        let mut rng_val: f32 = rand::random();\n        for (params, acc) in self.history.iter() {\n            rng_val -= *acc / total_acc;\n            if rng_val <= 0.0 {\n                return Some(params.clone());\n            }\n        }\n        self.history.back().map(|(p, _)| p.clone())\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl HyperparameterTuner for BayesianTuner {\n    async fn propose(\n        &mut self,\n        latest_metrics: &ModelMetrics,\n    ) -> Result<HyperParams> {\n        // Persist the last known good params and accuracy for future sampling.\n        if let Some(prev) = self.history.back() {\n            // Only store if the model is improving and the change is meaningful.\n            if latest_metrics.accuracy > prev.1 + 0.002 {\n                let mut entry = prev.clone();\n                entry.1 = latest_metrics.accuracy;\n                self.history.push_back(entry);\n                if self.history.len() > self.history_capacity {\n                    self.history.pop_front();\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Either sample near a historically good configuration or sample random.\n        let base = self.weighted_sample().unwrap_or_else(|| HyperParams::default());\n\n        // Jitter around the base parameters.\n        let lr_dist = Uniform::new(0.5, 1.5);\n        let wd_dist = Uniform::new(0.5, 1.5);\n        let aug_dist = Uniform::new(-0.1f32, 0.1f32);\n\n        let mut proposal = base.clone();\n        proposal.learning_rate *= lr_dist.sample(&mut self.rng);\n        proposal.weight_decay *= wd_dist.sample(&mut self.rng);\n        proposal.augmentation_prob =\n            (proposal.augmentation_prob + aug_dist.sample(&mut self.rng)).clamp(0.0, 1.0);\n        // Pick a nearby batch size (\u00b11 step).\n        proposal.batch_size = match self.rng.gen_range(0..=2) {\n            0 if proposal.batch_size > 8 => proposal.batch_size / 2,\n            2 => proposal.batch_size * 2,\n            _ => proposal.batch_size,\n        }\n        .clamp(8, 256);\n\n        Ok(proposal)\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"BayesianTuner\"\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                           Factory Pattern \u2013 Builder                        */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Enumeration of all supported tuner implementations.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy)]\npub enum TunerType {\n    Grid,\n    Bayesian,\n}\n\npub struct TunerFactory;\n\nimpl TunerFactory {\n    pub fn build(tuner: TunerType) -> Arc<Mutex<dyn HyperparameterTuner>> {\n        match tuner {\n            TunerType::Grid => Arc::new(Mutex::new(GridTuner::new())),\n            TunerType::Bayesian => Arc::new(Mutex::new(BayesianTuner::new())),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                 Auto-Tuning Service \u2013 End-to-End Orchestrator              */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Interval between automatic tuning rounds (default = 30 minutes).\nconst DEFAULT_TUNING_INTERVAL: Duration = Duration::from_secs(30 * 60);\n\n/// Service that connects the metrics stream with the tuner and emits new\n/// hyper-parameters whenever the strategy decides an update is needed.\n/// The produced configs are sent back to Model-Ops to trigger re-training.\npub struct AutoTuningService {\n    metrics_sub: broadcast::Receiver<ModelMetrics>,\n    tuner: Arc<Mutex<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>,\n    min_accuracy: f32,\n    max_latency_ms: f32,\n    interval: Duration,\n}\n\nimpl AutoTuningService {\n    /// Construct and wire the background service.\n    pub fn new(\n        publisher: MetricsPublisher,\n        tuner: Arc<Mutex<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>,\n        min_accuracy: f32,\n        max_latency_ms: f32,\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            metrics_sub: publisher.subscribe(),\n            tuner,\n            min_accuracy,\n            max_latency_ms,\n            interval: DEFAULT_TUNING_INTERVAL,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Adjustable interval mainly used in integration tests.\n    pub fn with_interval(mut self, interval: Duration) -> Self {\n        self.interval = interval;\n        self\n    }\n\n    /// Spawn the service in its own asynchronous task. The join-handle is\n    /// returned so the caller can manage lifecycle (e.g. cancel on shutdown).\n    pub fn spawn(self) -> tokio::task::JoinHandle<()> {\n        tokio::spawn(async move { self.run().await })\n    }\n\n    async fn run(mut self) {\n        let mut ticker = time::interval(self.interval);\n        let mut latest_metrics: Option<ModelMetrics> = None;\n\n        loop {\n            tokio::select! {\n                biased;\n\n                _ = ticker.tick() => {\n                    if let Some(metrics) = &latest_metrics {\n                        if metrics.is_good_enough(self.min_accuracy, self.max_latency_ms) {\n                            debug!(\"AutoTuningService: metrics already above threshold \u2013 skip round\");\n                            continue;\n                        }\n                        info!(\"AutoTuningService: triggering tuner `{}`\", self.tuner.lock().await.name());\n                        match self.tuner.lock().await.propose(metrics).await {\n                            Ok(new_params) => {\n                                // In production, we would invoke Model-Ops here.\n                                info!(\n                                    \"AutoTuningService: proposed new params: lr={:.5}, wd={:.5}, bs={}, aug={:.2}\",\n                                    new_params.learning_rate,\n                                    new_params.weight_decay,\n                                    new_params.batch_size,\n                                    new_params.augmentation_prob,\n                                );\n                                // TODO: send to training scheduler via gRPC/kafka/etc.\n                            }\n                            Err(err) => {\n                                error!(\"AutoTuningService: tuner error: {err:#}\");\n                            }\n                        }\n                    } else {\n                        debug!(\"AutoTuningService: no metrics yet \u2013 waiting\");\n                    }\n                }\n\n                // Receive metrics asynchronously; ignore errors when channel is lagging.\n                res = self.metrics_sub.recv() => match res {\n                    Ok(m) => {\n                        latest_metrics = Some(m);\n                    }\n                    Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Lagged(skipped)) => {\n                        warn!(\"AutoTuningService: skipped {skipped} lagged metric messages\");\n                    }\n                    Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Closed) => {\n                        warn!(\"AutoTuningService: metrics channel closed \u2013 terminating\");\n                        return;\n                          */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use tokio::time::timeout;\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn grid_tuner_exhausts() {\n        let mut tuner = GridTuner::new();\n        let dummy_metrics = ModelMetrics {\n            accuracy: 0.1,\n            latency_ms: Strategy, Factory, and Observer patterns to enable adaptive\n//! hyper-parameter tuning and automated retraining triggers.\n//!\n//! self.params.insert(key.into(), value);\n    }\n\n    pub fn get(&self, key: &str) -> Option<f64> {\n        self.params.get(key).cloned()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Training (or validation) metrics used as threshold_pct: f32,\n    tx_retrain: Sender<RetrainEvent>,\n    model_id: String,\n}\n\nimpl PerformanceMonitor {\n    /// Create a new monitor.\n    ///\n    /// * `window` \u2013 number of recent metrics used to compute rolling mean.\n    /// * `threshold_pct` \u2013 acceptable degradation percentage vs. best.\n    pub fn new(\n        model_id: String,\n        window: usize,\n        threshold_pct: f32,\n        tx_retrain: Sender<RetrainEvent>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            history: VecDeque::with_capacity(window),\n            window,\n            threshold_pct,\n            tx_retrain,\n            model_id,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Computes moving average loss over the internal window.\n    fn avg_loss(&self) -> Option<f32> {\n        if self.history.is_empty() {\n            return None;\n        }\n        Some(\n            self.history\n                .iter()\n                .map(|m| m.loss)\n                .sum::<f32>()\n                / self.history.len() as f32,\n        )\n    }\n}\n\nimpl MetricsObserver for PerformanceMonitor {\n    fn on_metrics_update(&mut self, metrics: &TrainingMetrics) {\n        // Maintain bounded window.\n        if self.history.len() == self.window {\n            self.history.pop_front();\n        }\n        self.history.push_back(*metrics);\n\n        // Compute rolling avg and detect degradation.\n        if let Some(avg_loss) = self.avg_loss() {\n            let worst_allowed = avg_loss * (1.0 + self.threshold_pct);\n            if metrics.loss > worst_allowed {\n                // Push retrain event.\n                let evt = RetrainEvent {\n                    model_id: self.model_id.clone(),\n                    reason: format!(\n                        \"Loss degraded {:.2}% vs. rolling mean\",\n                        (metrics.loss / avg_loss - 1.0) * 100.0\n                    ),\n                };\n                // It's okay to ignore send errors Consumes new metrics from `rx_metrics`.\n/// 2. Feeds them to the tuner.\n/// 3. Broadcasts them to observers.\n/// 4. Emits new hyper-parameter configs via `tx_config`.\npub struct TuningCoordinator {\n    tuner: Mutex<Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>,\n    observers: Mutex<Vec<Box<dyn MetricsObserver>>>,\n    rx_metrics: Receiver<(HyperParameterConfig, TrainingMetrics)>,\n    tx_config: Sender<HyperParameterConfig>,\n}\n\nimpl TuningCoordinator {\n    #[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]\n    pub fn new(\n        tuner: Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>,\n        observers: Vec<Box<dyn MetricsObserver>>,\n        rx_metrics: Receiver<(HyperParameterConfig, TrainingMetrics)>,\n        tx_config: Sender<HyperParameterConfig>,\n    ) -> Arc<Self> {\n        Arc::new(Self {\n            tuner: Mutex::new(tuner),\n            observers: Mutex::new(observers),\n            rx_metrics,\n            tx_config,\n        })\n    }\n\n    /// Blocking loop; should be spawned on its own thread / executor.\n    pub fn start(self: Arc<Self>) {\n        std::thread::spawn(move || {\n            let ticker = tick(Duration::from_secs(1));\n\n            loop {\n                select! {\n                    recv(self.rx_metrics) -> msg => {\n                        match msg {\n                            Ok((cfg, metrics)) => {\n                                // 1) Produce new config via tuner.\n                                let mut tuner = self.tuner.lock().expect(\"poisoned lock\");\n                                match tuner.tune(&cfg, &metrics) {\n                                    Ok(new_cfg) => {\n                                        // Send back to upstream training service\n                                        if let Err(err) = self.tx_config.send(new_cfg) {\n                                            eprintln!(\"TuningCoordinator: failed to send new config: {err}\");\n                                        }\n                                    }\n                                    Err(e) => eprintln!(\"TuningCoordinator: tune() failed: {e:?}\"),\n                                }\n\n                                // 2) Notify observers.\n                                for obs in self.observers.lock().expect(\"poisoned lock\").iter_mut() {\n                                    obs.on_metrics_update(&metrics);\n                                }\n                            }\n                            Err(_) => {\n                                // Upstream closed. Shutdown gracefully.\n                                break;\n                            }\n                        }\n                    }\n                    recv(ticker) -> _ => {\n                        // Heart-beat for logging / metrics integration.\n                        // In prod we would emit metrics to Prometheus here.\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        });\n    }\n}\n\n//\n// ---------- Self-contained Integration Test -------------------------------------------------------\n//\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn end_to_end_flow() {\n        // a) Wire channels.\n        let (tx_metrics, rx_metrics) = bounded::<(HyperParameterConfig, TrainingMetrics)>(4);\n        let (tx_cfg_out, rx_cfg_out) = bounded::<HyperParameterConfig>(4);\n        let (tx_retrain, _rx_retrain) = bounded::<RetrainEvent>(4);\n\n        // b) Concrete strategy + observer.\n        let tuner = TunerFactory::create(TunerKind::GridSearch);\n        let monitor = PerformanceMonitor::new(\"model-xyz\".into(), 4, 0.05, tx_retrain);\n\n        // c) Coordinator.\n        let coord = TuningCoordinator::new(tuner, vec![Box::new(monitor)], rx_metrics, tx_cfg_out);\n        coord.start();\n\n        // d) Push dummy metrics.\n        let mut cfg = HyperParameterConfig::new();\n        cfg.insert(\"lr\", 0.01);\n        cfg.insert(\"momentum\", 0.9);\n\n        for i in 0..5 {\n            let mut metrics = TrainingMetrics {\n                accuracy: 0.9,\n                f1_score: 0.92,\n                loss: 0.1 + i as f32 * 0.02,\n            };\n            tx_metrics.send((cfg.clone(), metrics)).unwrap();\n\n            // Receive tuned config.\n            let new_cfg = rx_cfg_out.recv().unwrap();\n            assert!(new_cfg.get(\"lr\").is_some());\n        }\n    }\n}\n```",

    "content": "```rust\n/*!\nModule 71 \u2013 Adaptive hyper-parameter tuning & experiment tracking\n\nThis module provides a production-grade implementation of:\n\n* Strategy Pattern \u2013 multiple `HyperparameterTuner` strategies at runtime\n* Observer Pattern  \u2013 `TrainingObserver` that receives callbacks from the\n  model-training engine and feeds metrics back into the tuner\n* Experiment tracking \u2013 light-weight SQLite persistence backed by `rusqlite`\n  for auditability\n\nThe module is self-contained and does not perform the actual model training.\nInstead, it exposes stable, async-friendly APIs that the higher-level\n`Model Ops` layer can call to obtain hyper-parameters and report training\nresults.\n\nThe public surface area is intentionally small so that it can be consumed\nfrom other language bindings (FFI), gRPC layers, or CLI tooling.\n*/\n\nuse std::collections::HashMap;\nuse std::path::{Path, PathBuf};\nuse std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\n\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result};\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse log::{debug, error, info, warn};\nuse rand::seq::SliceRandom;\nuse rand::{thread_rng, Rng};\nuse rusqlite::{params, Connection};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\n/// Common alias for hyper-parameter name/value mapping.\npub type HyperParams = HashMap<String, f64>;\n\n/// Strategy pattern: A tuner is responsible for suggesting the next set of\n/// hyper-parameters *and* ingesting the resulting score so that it can adapt\n/// its internal search.\n///\n/// Implementors must be `Send + Sync` so that the search can be distributed\n/// across threads or processes.\n///\n/// NOTE: The tuner does *not* execute the training job.  That responsibility\n/// lies with the `Model Ops` layer.  The tuner is also side-effect free\u2013\u2013\n/// apart from internal bookkeeping.\npub trait HyperparameterTuner: Send + Sync {\n    /// Suggest the next configuration to evaluate.\n    fn suggest(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams>;\n\n    /// Report the evaluation metric (e.g. accuracy, loss) for a previously\n    /// suggested configuration.  Implementations may choose to ignore the\n    /// score when the configuration is unknown.\n    fn report_result(&mut self, params: &HyperParams, metric: f64);\n\n    /// Human-readable name; useful for telemetry & debugging.\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n}\n\n/// A simple grid-search tuner that exhaustively evaluates the Cartesian\n/// product of discrete candidate values.\n///\n/// Useful for deterministic sweeps when the search space is small.\npub struct GridSearchTuner {\n    grid: Vec<HyperParams>,\n    cursor: usize,\n}\n\nimpl GridSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(candidates: HashMap<String, Vec<f64>>) -> Self {\n        // Compute Cartesian product\n        let mut grid: Vec<HyperParams> = vec![];\n        Self::cartesian_product(\n            &mut grid,\n            &mut HyperParams::new(),\n            &candidates.into_iter().collect::<Vec<_>>(),\n            0,\n        );\n        info!(\"GridSearch initialized with {} configurations\", grid.len());\n        Self { grid, cursor: 0 }\n    }\n\n    fn cartesian_product(\n        acc: &mut Vec<HyperParams>,\n        current: &mut HyperParams,\n        items: &[(String, Vec<f64>)],\n        idx: usize,\n    ) {\n        if idx == items.len() {\n            acc.push(current.clone());\n            return;\n        }\n\n        let (ref key, ref values) = items[idx];\n        for v in values {\n            current.insert(key.clone(), *v);\n            Self::cartesian_product(acc, current, items, idx + 1);\n        }\n        current.remove(key);\n    }\n}\n\nimpl HyperparameterTuner for GridSearchTuner {\n    fn suggest(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams> {\n        if self.cursor >= self.grid.len() {\n            None\n        } else {\n            let params = self.grid[self.cursor].clone();\n            self.cursor += 1;\n            Some(params)\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn report_result(&mut self, _params: &HyperParams, _metric: f64) {\n        // grid search is stateless; nothing to do.\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"GridSearchTuner\"\n    }\n}\n\n/// Random search tuner that samples uniformly from user-supplied ranges.\n/// Each range is inclusive.\n///\n/// NOTE: For continuous variables, the range is treated as continuous;\n/// for discrete variables, the caller can pass equal min==max to achieve\n/// deterministic behavior.\npub struct RandomSearchTuner {\n    ranges: HashMap<String, (f64, f64)>,\n    max_trials: usize,\n    trials: usize,\n    history: Vec<(HyperParams, f64)>,\n}\n\nimpl RandomSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(ranges: HashMap<String, (f64, f64)>, max_trials: usize) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            ranges,\n            max_trials,\n            trials: 0,\n            history: Vec::new(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn random_sample(&self) -> HyperParams {\n        let mut rng = thread_rng();\n        self.ranges\n            .iter()\n            .map(|(k, (min, max))| (k.clone(), rng.gen_range(*min..=*max)))\n            .collect()\n    }\n}\n\nimpl HyperparameterTuner for RandomSearchTuner {\n    fn suggest(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams> {\n        if self.trials >= self.max_trials {\n            None\n        } else {\n            self.trials += 1;\n            Some(self.random_sample())\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn report_result(&mut self, params: &HyperParams, metric: f64) {\n        self.history.push((params.clone(), metric));\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"RandomSearchTuner\"\n    }\n}\n\n/// Factory pattern: build tuners dynamically based on a string identifier.\n/// This allows runtime configuration via CLI, YAML, or remote control plane.\npub enum TunerFactory;\n\nimpl TunerFactory {\n    pub fn make_grid_search(candidates: HashMap<String, Vec<f64>>) -> Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner> {\n        Box::new(GridSearchTuner::new(candidates))\n    }\n\n    pub fn make_random_search(\n        ranges: HashMap<String, (f64, f64)>,\n        max_trials: usize,\n    ) -> Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner> {\n        Box::new(RandomSearchTuner::new(ranges, max_trials))\n    }\n}\n\n/// Observer pattern \u2013 The model-training engine emits `TrainingEvent`s that\n/// observers can subscribe to.  The tuner implementation itself can be an\n/// observer in order to implement adaptive search algorithms such as Bayesian\n/// optimization, however, we keep them decoupled so that multiple observers\n/// (e.g. loggers, alerting) can co-exist.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub enum TrainingEvent {\n    EpochStart { epoch: u32 },\n    EpochEnd {\n        epoch: u32,\n        metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n    },\n    TrainingFinish {\n        best_metric: f64,\n        best_params: HyperParams,\n    },\n}\n\n/// Observer trait.\npub trait TrainingObserver: Send + Sync {\n    fn on_event(&self, event: &TrainingEvent);\n}\n\n/// Default implementation that feeds back the final metric to the tuner.\npub struct TunerObserver {\n    tuner: Arc<Mutex<Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>>,\n}\n\nimpl TunerObserver {\n    pub fn new(tuner: Arc<Mutex<Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>>) -> Self {\n        Self { tuner }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl TrainingObserver for TunerObserver {\n    fn on_event(&self, event: &TrainingEvent) {\n        if let TrainingEvent::TrainingFinish {\n            best_metric,\n            best_params,\n        } = event\n        {\n            if let Ok(mut tuner) = self.tuner.lock() {\n                tuner.report_result(best_params, *best_metric);\n            } else {\n                error!(\"Unable to lock tuner mutex in observer\");\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Lightweight experiment tracking backed by SQLite.\n/// Production deployments can replace this with a more\n/// sophisticated store (Postgres, Influx, etc.) via\n/// feature flags without changing the public API.\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub struct ExperimentTracker {\n    db_path: PathBuf,\n    conn: Connection,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ExperimentRecord {\n    pub id: i64,\n    pub timestamp: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub tuner_name: String,\n    pub params: HyperParams,\n    pub metric: f64,\n}\n\nimpl ExperimentTracker {\n    /// Create a new tracker with the given file path.\n    pub fn new<P: AsRef<Path>>(db_path: P) -> Result<Self> {\n        let conn = Connection::open(&db_path)\n            .with_context(|| format!(\"opening experiments db {:?}\", db_path.as_ref()))?;\n\n        let tracker = Self {\n            db_path: db_path.as_ref().to_path_buf(),\n            conn,\n        };\n\n        tracker.init_schema()?;\n        Ok(tracker)\n    }\n\n    fn init_schema(&self) -> Result<()> {\n        self.conn.execute_batch(\n            \"\n            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS experiments (\n                id          INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,\n                timestamp   TEXT NOT NULL,\n                tuner_name  TEXT NOT NULL,\n                params      BLOB NOT NULL,\n                metric      REAL NOT NULL\n            );\n            \",\n        )?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Persist an experiment record.\n    pub fn log_record(&self, tuner_name: &str, params: &HyperParams, metric: f64) -> Result<i64> {\n        let timestamp: DateTime<Utc> = Utc::now();\n        let params_blob = serde_json::to_vec(params).context(\"serializing hyperparams\")?;\n\n        self.conn.execute(\n            \"\n            INSERT INTO experiments (timestamp, tuner_name, params, metric)\n            VALUES (?1, ?2, ?3, ?4);\n            \",\n            params![\n                timestamp.to_rfc3339(),\n                tuner_name,\n                params_blob,\n                metric\n            ],\n        )?;\n\n        Ok(self.conn.last_insert_rowid())\n    }\n\n    /// Retrieve all experiments for auditing or analytics.\n    pub fn all_records(&self) -> Result<Vec<ExperimentRecord>> {\n        let mut stmt = self.conn.prepare(\n            \"\n            SELECT id, timestamp, tuner_name, params, metric\n            FROM experiments\n            ORDER BY id ASC;\n            \",\n        )?;\n\n        let iter = stmt.query_map([], |row| {\n            let params_blob: Vec<u8> = row.get(3)?;\n            let params: HyperParams = serde_json::from_slice(&params_blob)\n                .map_err(|e| rusqlite::Error::FromSqlConversionFailure(3, rusqlite::types::Type::Blob, Box::new(e)))?;\n\n            Ok(ExperimentRecord {\n                id: row.get(0)?,\n                timestamp: DateTime::parse_from_rfc3339(&row.get::<_, String>(1)?)\n                    .map(|dt| dt.with_timezone(&Utc))\n                    .map_err(|e| rusqlite::Error::FromSqlConversionFailure(1, rusqlite::types::Type::Text, Box::new(e)))?,\n                tuner_name: row.get(2)?,\n                params,\n                metric: row.get(4)?,\n            })\n        })?;\n\n        let mut out = Vec::new();\n        for rec in iter {\n            out.push(rec?);\n        }\n        Ok(out)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Example of orchestrating an end-to-end hyper-parameter tuning session.\n/// The function is *sync* for brevity but can be made async using\n/// `tokio::task::spawn_blocking` or similar.\n///\n/// NOTE: This is *not* executed automatically; it serves as a reference\n/// implementation for higher-level orchestration code.\npub fn run_hpo_session() -> Result<()> {\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    // Create the tuner (here: grid search)\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    let mut candidates: HashMap<String, Vec<f64>> = HashMap::new();\n    candidates.insert(\"learning_rate\".into(), vec![0.01, 0.001]);\n    candidates.insert(\"dropout\".into(), vec![0.1, 0.2, 0.3]);\n\n    let tuner: Arc<Mutex<Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>> =\n        Arc::new(Mutex::new(TunerFactory::make_grid_search(candidates)));\n\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    // Initialize experiment tracker\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    let tracker = ExperimentTracker::new(\"experiments.db\")?;\n\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    // Main loop\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    loop {\n        let next_params = {\n            let mut tuner = tuner.lock().expect(\"tuner lock poisoned\");\n            tuner.suggest()\n        };\n\n        let Some(params) = next_params else {\n            info!(\"Hyper-parameter search complete.\");\n            break;\n        };\n\n        // ------------------------------------------------------------------\n        // >>>>  In the real system, `train_model()` would kick off an *async*\n        // >>>>  training job, possibly on a GPU worker pool and stream back\n        // >>>>  metrics over a channel.  For demonstration, we simulate a\n        // >>>>  random metric here.\n        // ------------------------------------------------------------------\n        let simulated_metric: f64 = poisoned\");\n            tuner_locked.report_result(&params, simulated_metric);\n        }\n\n        tracker\n            .log_record(\"GridSearchTuner\", &params, simulated_metric)\n            .context(\"logging experiment\")?;\n\n        debug!(\n            \"Evaluated {:?} -> metric = {:.4}\",\n            &params, simulated_metric\n        );\n    }\n\n    Ok(())\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod (\"batch_size\".to_string(), (16.0, 128.0)),\n        ]);\n\n        let mut tuner = RandomSearchTuner::new(ranges, 5);\n        let p1 = tuner.suggest().unwrap();\n        tuner.report_result(&p1, 0.92);\n        assert_eq!(tuner.trials, 1);\n        assert_eq!(tuner.history.len(), 1);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_grid_search_exhaustive() {\n        let mut can = HashMap::new();\n        can.insert(\"a\".into(), vec![1.0, 2.0]);\n        can.insert(\"b\".into(), vec![10.0]);\n\n        let mut tuner = GridSearchTuner::new(can);\n        assert!(tuner.suggest().is_some());\n spawn_dispatch_loop(\n        monitor: Arc<ModelMonitor>,\n        mut rx: UnboundedReceiver<ModelEvent>,\n        _buffer: usize,\n    ) {\n        task::spawn(async move {\n            while let deregister_observer(&mut self, obs_id: usize) {\n        let mut guard = self\n            .observers\n            .write()\n            .expect(\"ModelMonitor observer lock poisoned\");\n        if obs_id < guard.len() {\n            guard.remove(obs_id);\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn notify(&self, event: ModelEvent) {\n        let guard = self\n            .observers\n            .read()\n            .expect(\"ModelMonitor observer lock poisoned\");\n        for obs in guard.iter() {\n            // Fire & forget; each observer must handle its own failure modes\n            let evt = );\n\n        let mut rng = rand::thread_rng();\n        let range = Uniform::new(0.0, 1.0);\n        let mut best_score = 0.0;\n        let mut best_params = HashMap::new();\n\n        for trial in Hyperparameter-Tuning & Experiment-Tracking subsystem for VisuTility\n//! Orchestrator.  This module lives inside the `Feature Ops / Model Ops` layers\n//! and is responsible for proposing hyper-parameter candidates, capturing their\n//! evaluation metrics, and broadcasting events that can be consumed by other\n//! system components (e.g. the automated-retraining daemon).\n//!\n//! Architectural patterns used\n//! ---------------------------\n//! \u2022 Strategy Pattern \u2013 concrete `Tuner` implementations (Grid, Random, \u2026) share\n//!   a common `Tuner` trait.\n//! \u2022 Factory Pattern  \u2013 `TunerFactory` produces a concrete strategy at runtime\n//!   from high-level configuration.\n//! \u2022 Observer Pattern \u2013 `EventBus` enables decoupled metric listeners.\n//!\n//! External crates (add to Cargo.toml)\n//! -----------------------------------\n//! rand        = \"0.8\"\n//! serde       = { version = \"1\", features = [\"derive\"] }\n//! thiserror   = \"1\"\n//! chrono      = { version = \"0.4\", features = [\"serde\"] }\n//! log         = \"0.4\"\n//! parking_lot = \"0.12\"\n//! -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! NOTE:  This file purposefully avoids referencing any \u201cdeep-learny\u201d code; the\n//!        idea is that a caller feeds candidates to a model-training routine\n//!        and then invokes `update_result` with an obtained metric.\n//! -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nuse std::{\n    collections::{BTreeMap, HashMap, HashSet},\n    fs::{File, OpenOptions},\n    io::{BufWriter, Write},\n    path::Path,\n    sync::Arc,\n};\n\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse parking_lot::RwLock;\nuse rand::{seq::SliceRandom, Rng};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\n\n/// Result alias to simplify signatures throughout this module.\ntype Result<T> = std::result::Result<T, TuningError>;\n\n/// Domain-level errors surfaced by the hyper-parameter sub-system.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum TuningError {\n    #[error(\"parameter `{0}` is missing\")]\n    MissingParameter(String),\n\n    #[error(\"exhausted parameter space\")]\n    ExhaustedSpace,\n\n    #[error(\"IO error: {0}\")]\n    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    SerdeJson(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n}\n\n/// Primitive value supported in the parameter space.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize, PartialEq)]\n#[serde(untagged)]\npub enum ParamValue {\n    Int(i64),\n    Float(f64),\n    Str(String),\n}\n\nimpl std::fmt::Display for ParamValue {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {\n        match self {\n            ParamValue::Int(v) => write!(f, \"{v}\"),\n            ParamValue::Float(v) => write!(f, \"{v:.4}\"),\n            ParamValue::Str(v) => write!(f, \"{v}\"),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Parameter search space definition.  Each parameter maps to a set of allowed\n/// values.  Non-unique vectors are tolerated (for weighted search in future).\npub type ParamSpace = HashMap<String, Vec<ParamValue>>;\n\n/// A concrete candidate (single point) sampled from the parameter space.\npub type Candidate = BTreeMap<String, ParamValue /* ordered for stable hashing */>;\n\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Strategy Pattern: core trait implemented by concrete tuners.\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\npub trait Tuner: Send {\n    /// Produce the next candidate to evaluate.\n    fn next_candidate(&mut self) -> Result<Candidate>;\n\n    /// Notify the tuner that `score` (e.g. validation loss) was obtained for\n    /// `candidate`.  The tuner may use this information for adaptive search.\n    fn update_result(&mut self, candidate: &Candidate, score: f64) -> Result<()>;\n}\n\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Grid-Search implementation\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\npub struct GridSearchTuner {\n    space: ParamSpace,\n    cursor: Vec<usize>,\n    finished: bool,\n}\n\nimpl GridSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(space: ParamSpace) -> Self {\n        let cursor = vec![0; space.len()];\n        Self {\n            space,\n            cursor,\n            finished: false,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Helper for mapping the internal cursor into a concrete `Candidate`.\n    fn cursor_to_candidate(&self) -> Candidate {\n        let mut cand = Candidate::new();\n        for ((key, values), idx) in self.space.iter().zip(self.cursor.iter()) {\n            cand.insert(key.clone(), values[*idx].clone());\n        }\n        cand\n    }\n\n    /// Advances the multi-dimensional cursor.  Returns `false` if wrapped-around\n    /// and the entire grid was already enumerated.\n    fn increment_cursor(&mut self) -> bool {\n        for (dim_idx, (_, values)) in self.space.iter().enumerate().rev() {\n            let limit = values.len();\n            self.cursor[dim_idx] += 1;\n            if self.cursor[dim_idx] < limit {\n                return true; // simple increment in this dimension\n            } else {\n                self.cursor[dim_idx] = 0; // carry-over to higher dimension\n            }\n        }\n        false // all dimensions wrapped\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Tuner for GridSearchTuner {\n    fn next_candidate(&mut self) -> Result<Candidate> {\n        if self.finished {\n            return Err(TuningError::ExhaustedSpace);\n        }\n        let cand = self.cursor_to_candidate();\n        if !self.increment_cursor() {\n            self.finished = true;\n        }\n        Ok(cand)\n    }\n\n    fn update_result(&mut self, _candidate: &Candidate, _score: f64) -> Result<()> {\n        // Grid search is exhaustive & non-adaptive \u2192 nothing to do.\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Random-Search implementation\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\npub struct RandomSearchTuner {\n    space: ParamSpace,\n    seen_hashes: HashSet<u64>, // prevent duplicates\n    max_trials: Option<usize>,\n}\n\nimpl RandomSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(space: ParamSpace, max_trials: Option<usize>) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            space,\n            seen_hashes: HashSet::new(),\n            max_trials,\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn sample_candidate<R: Rng + ?Sized>(&self, rng: &mut R) -> Candidate {\n        let mut cand = Candidate::new();\n        for (k, vals) in &self.space {\n            let choice = vals.choose(rng).expect(\"non-empty param values\");\n            cand.insert(k.clone(), choice.clone());\n        }\n        cand\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Tuner for RandomSearchTuner {\n    fn next_candidate(&mut self) -> Result<Candidate> {\n        if let Some(limit) = self.max_trials {\n            if self.seen_hashes.len() >= limit {\n                return Err(TuningError::ExhaustedSpace);\n            }\n        }\n\n        let mut rng = rand::thread_rng();\n        for _ in 0..1000 {\n            let cand = self.sample_candidate(&mut rng);\n            let hash = fxhash::hash64(&cand);\n            if self.seen_hashes.insert(hash) {\n                return Ok(cand);\n            }\n        }\n        Err(TuningError::ExhaustedSpace)\n    }\n\n    fn update_result(&mut self, _candidate: &Candidate, _score: f64) -> Result<()> {\n        // Could implement adaptive sampling (Bayesian etc.) later.\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Factory Pattern: create concrete tuner from a lightweight config enum.\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n#[derive(Clone, Debug)]\npub enum TunerKind {\n    Grid,\n    Random { max_trials: Option<usize> },\n}\n\npub struct TunerFactory;\n\nimpl TunerFactory {\n    pub fn build(kind: TunerKind, space: ParamSpace) -> Box<dyn Tuner> {\n        match kind {\n            TunerKind::Grid => Box::new(GridSearchTuner::new(space)),\n            TunerKind::Random { max_trials } => Box::new(RandomSearchTuner::new(space, max_trials)),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Observer Pattern: EventBus for publishing & subscribing to metric events.\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Event emitted after a trial is finished.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize)]\npub struct TrialFinishedEvent {\n    pub candidate: Candidate,\n    pub score: f64,\n    pub finished_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n}\n\n/// Simple, in-process event bus backed by `parking_lot::RwLock`.\n#[derive(Default)]\npub struct EventBus {\n    listeners: RwLock<Vec<Arc<dyn Fn(&TrialFinishedEvent) + Send + Sync>>>,\n}\n\nimpl EventBus {\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        Self::default()\n    }\n\n    /// Subscribe a listener callback.  Returns a handle that can be `drop`ped to\n    /// unsubscribe (implemented via `Arc` ref-counting).\n    pub fn subscribe<F>(&self, listener: F) -> Arc<dyn Fn(&TrialFinishedEvent) + Send + Sync>\n    where\n        F: Fn(&TrialFinishedEvent) + Send + Sync + 'static,\n    {\n        let arc = Arc::new(listener);\n        self.listeners.write().push(arc.clone());\n        arc\n    }\n\n    pub fn dispatch(&self, evt: TrialFinishedEvent) {\n        for listener in self.listeners.read().iter() {\n            listener(&evt);\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Experiment Tracker\n/// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\npub trait ExperimentTracker: Send + Sync {\n    fn log_trial(&self, evt: &TrialFinishedEvent) -> Result<()>;\n}\n\n/// Tracker that appends each trial as JSON to a local file.\n/// Suitable for on-prem installations without an external tracking service.\npub struct LocalFileTracker {\n    file: RwLock<BufWriter<File>>,\n}\n\nimpl LocalFileTracker {\n    pub fn open<P: AsRef<Path>>(path: P) ->
